Jamison Brereton

35
Savitar (except Agni, Mitra and Varun╠гa, Ra╠Дtr─л, and Savitar 1)
Hiraс╣Зyast┼лpa ─Ас╣Еgirasa
11 verses: triс╣гс╣нubh, except jagat─л 1, 9
After an initial verse invoking several gods, Savitar becomes the sole focus of the hymnтАФSavitar primarily in his role as god of the evening, as was already suggested by the invocation of Night in verse 1c. The first part of the Savitar portion (vss. 2тАУ5) describes the beauty of SavitarтАЩs chariot and his journey through the night sky. During this journey he (and his horses, vss. 2 and 5; see also 7тАУ8) survey the crea tures and the larger cosmos in which they live, and in the second part of the hymn (vss. 6тАУ9) we learn what was seen. These verses enumerate the parts of the cosmos and sketch its dimensions. This section is presented as mystical instruction (see esp. vs. 6d), which raises cosmic questions (vs. 7cd), especially about what happens to the sun during the night that Savitar is presiding over. The anxieties raised by the absence of the sun are put to rest by SavitarтАЩs ability to pervade the whole realm (vs. 9), and the hymn ends with an invitation to the god to come to us along his well
maintained route through the midspace (vss. 10тАУ11).

Jamison Brereton Notes

тАЬInvoke Agni first, for protection: I invoke for protection, Mitra and Varuс╣Зa; invoke Night, who brings rest to the world; invoke the divine Savit─Б for my preservation.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

I invoke Agni first, for well-being; I invoke Mitra and Varuс╣Зa here, for help. I invoke Night, who brings to rest the moving; I invoke god Savitar, for aid.

Griffith

AGNI I first invoke for our prosperity; I call on Mitra, Varuna, to aid us here.
I call on Night who gives rest to all moving life; I call on Savitar the God to lend us help.

Geldner

Ich rufe zuerst den Agni zum Heil, ich rufe Mitra und Varuna hierher zum Beistand. Ich rufe die Nacht, die alles Lebende zur Ruhe bringt, ich rufe den Gott Savitri zur Hilfe.

Grassmann

Ich ruf zuerst den Agni an zum Wohlergehn, ich rufe Mitra-Varuna zur H├╝lfe her; Ich ruf’ die Nacht, die, was da lebt, zur Ruhe legt, Ich rufe her zum Beistand Savitar, den Gott.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬRevolving through the darkened firmament, arousing mortal and immortal, the divine Savit─Б travels in his golden chariot, beholding the (several) worlds.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Turning hither through the black realm, bringing to rest the immortal and the mortal,
with his golden chariot Savitar the god drives here, gazing upon the creatures.

Griffith

Throughout the dusky firmament advancing, laying to rest the immortal and the mortal,
Borne in his golden chariot he cometh, Savitar, God who looks on every creature.

Geldner

Indem er mit dem schwarzen Dunst sich heranbewegt und Gott und Mensch zur Ruhe bringt, kommt Gott Savitri auf goldenem Wagen, die Wesen beschauend.

Grassmann

Er, der herbeieilt durch den dunklen Luftraum, zur Ruhe legt, was sterblich, was unsterblich, Gott Savitar auf seinem goldnen Wagen kommt her zu uns, beschauend alle Wesen.

Elizarenkova

рджреЗрд╡рдГ рджреАрдкреНрдпрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╡рддрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдгрд╡рддрд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдг рдпрд╛рддрд┐ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ред рддрдерд╛ рдЙрджреНрд╡рддрд╛ рдЙрддреНрдХреГрд╖реНрдЯреЗрдиреЛрд░реНрдзреНрд╡рджреЗрд╢рдпреБрдХреНрддреЗрди рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧреЗрдг рдпрд╛рддрд┐ ред рдЙрджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрддрд░рдВ рдордзреНрдпрд╛рд╣реНрдирдореВрд░реНрдзреНрд╡реЛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрдГ; рддрдд рдЙрдкрд░рд┐ рдЖрд╕рд╛рдпрдВ рдкреНрд░рд╡рдгреЛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рд╡реЗрдХрдГ ред рддрдерд╛ рдпрдЬрддрдГ рдпрд╖реНрдЯрд╡реНрдпрдГ рд╕ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рд╢реБрднреНрд░рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╢реНрд╡реЗрддрд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН рдЕрд╢реНрд╡рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдВ рдпрд╛рддрд┐ рджреЗрд╡рдпрдЬрдирджреЗрд╢реЗ рдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ ред рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рджреЗрд╡рдГ рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡рд╛рдгрд┐ рдкрд╛рдкрд╛рдирд┐ рдЕрдк рдмрд╛рдзрдорд╛рдирдГ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢рдпрдиреН рдкрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдГ рджреВрд░рджреЗрд╢рд╛рддреН ред рдкрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдГ ’ (рдирд┐. рей. реирем. рел) рдЗрддрд┐ рджреВрд░рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рдкрдард┐рддрддреНрд╡рд╛рддреН ред рддрд╛рджреГрд╢рд╛рддреН рджреНрдпреБрд▓реЛрдХрд╛рддреН рдЖ рдпрд╛рддрд┐ рдпрд╛рдЧрджреЗрд╢реЗ рдЖрдЧрдЪреНрдЫрддрд┐ рее рдкреНрд░рд╡рддрд╛ ред тАв рд╡рди рд╖рдг рд╕рдВрднрдХреНрддреМ ред рдЕрд╕реНрдорд╛рддреН рдкреНрд░рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рддреН рдХреНрд╡рд┐рдкреН ред тАШрдЧрдорд╛рджреАрдирд╛рдорд┐рддрд┐ рд╡рдХреНрддрд╡реНрдпрдореН’ (рдкрд╛. рд╕реВ. рем. рек. рекреж. рез) рдЗрддреНрдпрдиреБрдирд╛рд╕рд┐рдХрд▓реЛрдкрдГред рддрддрдГ рддреБрдХреН ред рдХреГрджреБрддреНрддрд░рдкрдж рдкреНрд░рдХреГрддрд┐рд╕реНрд╡рд░рддреНрд╡рдореН ред рдЙрджреНрд╡рддрд╛ ред рдЙрддреНрдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╛рддреН рд╡рдирддреЗрдГ рдкреВрд░реНрд╡рд╡рддреНрдкреНрд░рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛ ред рдпрдЬрддрдГ ред рднреГрдореГрджреГрд╢рд┐’ (рдЙ. рд╕реВ. рей. рейрепреж) рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджрд┐рдирд╛ рдпрдЬрддреЗрдГ рдХрд░реНрдордгрд┐ рдЕрддрдЪреНрдкреНрд░рддреНрдпрдпрдГ ред рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛ рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛ ред рдЙрднрдпрддреНрд░ тАШрд╢реЗрд╢реНрдЫрдиреНрджрд╕рд┐ рдмрд╣реБрд▓рдореН’ рдЗрддрд┐ рд╢реЗрд░реНрд▓реЛрдкрдГ рее

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe divine Savit─Б travels by an upward and by a downward path; deserving adoration, he journeys with two white horses; he comes hither from a distance, removing all sins.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The god drives on a downward slope; he drives on an upward one; he drives with two resplendent fallow bays, he who is worthy of the
sacrifice.
God Savitar drives hither from afar, thrusting away all obstacles.

Griffith

The God moves by the upward path, the downward; with two bright Bays, adorable, he journeys.
Savitar comes, the God from the far distance, and chases from us all distress and sorrow.

Geldner

Grassmann

Es f├дhrt der Gott die H├╢hn herab, die H├╢hn herauf mit hellem, goldnem Rossepaar, der heilige, Aus weiter Ferne kommt Gott Savitar herbei, weit von uns alles Ungemach verjagend.

Elizarenkova

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рд╡рд┐рд╖рдпрдГ

рдЕрдм рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдФрд░ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдп рдХреЗ рджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрдд рдХреЗ рд╕рд╛рде рдЕрдЧрд▓реЗ рдордиреНрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░ рдХреЗ рдЧреБрдгреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рд╣реИред

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдиреНрд╡рдпрднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЬреИрд╕реЗ (рд╡рд┐рд╢реНрд╡рд╛) рд╕рдм (рджреБрд░рд┐рддрд╛) рджреБрд╖реНрдЯ рджреБрдГрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЕрдк) (рдмрд╛рдзрдорд╛рдирдГ) рджреВрд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рдпрдЬрддрдГ) рд╕рдВрдЧрдо рдХрд░рдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рджреЗрд╡рдГ) рд╢реНрд░рд╡рдг рдЖрджрд┐ рдЬреНрдЮрд╛рди рдХрд╛ рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХ рд╡рд╛рдпреБ (рдкреНрд░рд╡рддрд╛) рдиреАрдЪреЗ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рд╕реЗ (рдпрд╛рддрд┐) рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рдЖрддрд╛ рдФрд░ (рдЙрджреНрд╡рддрд╛) рдКрд░реНрдзреНрд╡ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рд╕реЗ (рдпрд╛рддрд┐) рдЬрд╛рддрд╛ рдЖрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рд╕рдм рджреБрдГрдЦ рджреЗрдиреЗрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЕрдВрдзрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджрд┐рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рджреВрд░ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ (рдпрдЬрддрдГ) рд╕рдВрдЧрдд рд╣реЛрдиреЗ рдпреЛрдЧреНрдп (рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛) рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд╢рдХ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХ (рд╢реБрднреНрд░рд╛рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рд╢реБрджреНрдз (рд╣рд░рд┐рднреНрдпрд╛рдореН) рдХреГрд╖реНрдг рд╡рд╛ рд╢реБрдХреНрд▓рдкрдХреНрд╖реЛрдВ рд╕реЗ (рдкрд░рд╛рд╡рддрдГ) рджреБрд░рд╕реНрде рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдЕрдкрдиреА рдХрд┐рд░рдгреЛрдВ рд╕реЗ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрдХрд░ рдкреГрдерд┐рд╡реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рд▓реЛрдХреЛрдВ рдХреЛ (рдЖрдпрд╛рддрд┐) рд╕рдм рдкреНрд░рдХрд╛рд░ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдкреНрдд рд╣реЛрддрд╛ рд╣реИ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░рд╛рджрд┐ рд▓реЛрдЧ рд╕реЗрдирд╛ рдЖрджрд┐ рд╕рд╛рдордЧреНрд░реА рд╕рд╣рд┐рдд рдКрдВрдЪреЗ-рдиреАрдЪреЗ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдореЗрдВ рдЬрд╛-рдЖрдХреЗ рд╢рддреНрд░реБрдУрдВ рдХреЛ рдЬреАрддрдХрд░ рдкреНрд░рдЬрд╛ рдХреА рд░рдХреНрд╖рд╛ рдирд┐рд░рдиреНрддрд░ рдХрд┐рдпрд╛ рдХрд░реЗрдВ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рдЗрд╕ рдордВрддреНрд░ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдЪрдХрд▓реБрдкреНрддреЛрдкрдорд╛рд▓рдЩреНрдХрд╛рд░ рд╣реИред рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рдХреА рдЙрддреНрдкрдиреНрди рдХреА рд╣реБрдИ рд╕реГрд╖реНрдЯрд┐ рдореЗрдВ рд╡рд╛рдпреБ рдиреАрдЪреЗ рдКрдкрд░ рд╡рд╛ рд╕рдордЧрддрд┐ рд╕реЗ рдЪрд▓рддрд╛ рд╣реБрдЖ рдиреАрдЪреЗ рдХреЗ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдКрдкрд░ рдФрд░ рдКрдкрд░ рдХреЗ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдереЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдиреАрдЪреЗ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рдФрд░ рдЬреИрд╕реЗ рджрд┐рди рд░рд╛рдд рд╡рд╛ рдЖрдХрд░реНрд╖рдг рдзрд╛рд░рдг рдЧреБрдгрд╡рд╛рд▓реЗ рдЕрдкрдиреЗ рдХрд┐рд░рдг рд╕рдореВрд╣ рд╕реЗ рдпреБрдХреНрдд рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХ рдЕрдиреНрдзрдХрд╛рд░рд╛рджрд┐рдХреЛрдВ рдХреЗ рджреВрд░ рдХрд░рдиреЗ рд╕реЗ рджреБрдГрдЦреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░ рд╕реБрдЦ рдФрд░ рд╕реБрдЦреЛрдВ рдХрд╛ рд╡рд┐рдирд╛рд╢ рдХрд░ рджреБрдГрдЦреЛрдВ рдХреЛ рдкреНрд░рдЧрдЯ рдХрд░рддрд╛ рд╣реИ рд╡реИрд╕реЗ рд╣реА рд╕рднрд╛рдкрддрд┐ рдЖрджрд┐ рдХреЛ рднреА рдЕрдиреБрд╖реНрдард╛рди рдХрд░рдирд╛ рдЪрд╛рд╣рд┐рдпреЗ реерейрее

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдЕрде рд╡рд╛рдпреБрд╕реВрд░реНрдпреНрдпрджреГрд╖реНрдЯрд╛рдиреНрддреЗрди рд╢реВрд░рд╡реАрд░рдЧреБрдгрд╛ рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗред

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe many-rayed adorable Savit─Б, having power (to disperse) darkness from the world, has mounted his nigh-standing chariot, decorated with many kinds of golden ornaments, and furnished with golden yokes.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

(It is) covered over with pearls, having every beauty, with golden yoke-pins, loftyтАФ
his chariot has bright-beamed Savitar mounted, (he) worthy of the sacrifice, having assumed his own power throughout the black
realms.

Jamison Brereton Notes

I take kс╣Ыс╣гс╣З─Б╠Бr├бj─Бс╣Гsi loosely as an accusative of extent. Others (Geldner, Renou) supply a verb to govern this phrase (тАШverbreitendтАЩ and тАШpour traverserтАЭ respectively), while still others (Macdonell, Falk 1988, Witzel Got┼Н) take it as a second acc. with d├бdh─Бnaс╕е, as appositive to t├бviс╣г─лm тАЬassuming the dark realms as his power.тАЭ This latter solution is possible grammatically and does not require additional material to be supplied, but I am somewhat dubious that the dark realms constitute his power.

Griffith

His chariot decked with pearl, of various colours, lofty, with golden pole, the God hath mounted,
The many-rayed One, Savitar the holy, bound, bearing power and might, for darksome regions.

Savitri, der Anbetungsw├╝rdige, hat den perlenbedeckten, allfarbigen hohen Wagen mit goldenen Jochpfl├╢cken bestiegen, der Buntstrahlende, den schwarzen Dunst verbreitend, seine St├дrke anlegend.

Grassmann

Den perlgeschm├╝ckten, allgestalt’gen Wagen, mit goldnem Joch den hohen hat bestiegen In hellem Glanze Savitar, der hehre, im dunklen Luftraum seine Kraft erweisend.

Elizarenkova

тАЬHis white-footed coursers, harnessed to his car with a golden yoke, have manifested light to manking. Men and all the regions are ever in the presence of divine Savit─Б.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The dusky (horses) with white feet have looked out across the peoples, while drawing his chariot with its golden forepole.
The clans, all the creatures ever abide in the lap of divine Savitar.

Griffith

Drawing the gold-yoked car his Bays, white-footed, have manifested light to all the peoples.
Held in the lap of Savitar, divine One, all men, all beings have their place for ever.

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThree are the spheres; two are in the proximity of Savit─Б, one leads men to the dwelling of Yama. The immortal (luminaries) depend upon Savit─Б as a car upon the pin of the axle; let him who knows (the greatness of Savit─Б) declare it.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Amс╣Ыta = immortals; moon and constellations are added

Jamison Brereton

There are three heavens: two are the laps of Savitar, one is the
hero-vanquishing one in the world of Yama.
Like a chariot (wheel) on the axle-pin, the (creatures) have taken their place on his immortal (foundations?).тАФWhoever will perceive this, let him declare it here.

Jamison Brereton Notes

This verse of cosmic mystery decked out in numerology comes as a surprise after the simple, descriptive beginning of this hymn. The syntax of c is ambiguous: Geldner (Renou / Witzel Got┼Н) takes amс╣Ы╠Бt─Б as nom. pl., supplying тАЬhimтАЭ as acc. with ├бdhi тИЪsth─Б: тАЬAlles Unsterbliche ruht (auf ihm)тАжтАЭ I follow Oldenberg, who takes it as acc. pl., citing III.38.4 ─Б╠Бvi┼Ыv├бr┼лpo amс╣Ы╠Бt─Бni tasthau тАЬHaving all forms, he mounted on the immortal (things?).тАЭ

Griffith

Three heavens there are; two Savitar’s, adjacent: in Yama’s world is one, the home of heroes,
As on a linch-pin, firm, rest things immortal: he who hath known it let him here declare it.

Geldner

Drei Himmel gibt es, zwei sind der Scho├Я des Savitri, der eine ist in der Welt des Yama, der m├дnnerbezwingende. Alles Unsterbliche ruht auf ihm wie das Wagengestell auf den Achsbolzen. Wer das begriffen hat, soll es hier sagen.

Grassmann

Drei Himmel sind’s: des Savitar zwei Sitze, in Jama’s Reich der dritte, M├дnner hegend; Die G├╢tter ruhn wie auf der Wagenachse; wer das erkannt hat, m├╢g’ es hier verk├╝nden.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬSuparс╣Зa, (the solar ray), deep-quivering, life-bestowing, well-directed, has illuminated the three regions. Where now is S┼лrya Who knows to what sphere his rays have extended?тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

Supraс╣Зa = well-winged, a synonym of ra┼Ыmi, a ray; asura, from asu, vital breath; ra, who gives, hence life-giving

Jamison Brereton

The eagle has surveyed the midspacesтАФthe lord possessing profound inspiration, who gives good guidance.
Where now is the sun? Who perceives it? To which one of the heavens does his rein extend?

Jamison Brereton Notes

In some ways a responsive verse to the previous one(s): v├н тАж akhyat (a) parallels 5a v├н тАж akhyan; ciketa (c) responds to c├нketat in 6d; and the three heavens of 6a are alluded to in the query in 7d katam─Б╠Бс╣Г dy─Б╠Бm тАЬto which heaven (of three or more)?тАЭ

Griffith

He, strong of wing, hath lightened up the regions, deep-quivering Asura, the gentle Leader.
Where now is Surya, where is one to tell us to what celestial sphere his ray hath wandered?

Der sch├╢n beschwingte hat erhellt die L├╝fte, der tieferregte Gott, der herrlich leitet, Wo weilet jetzt der Sonnengott? wer weiss es? und welchen Himmel hat sein Strahl durchdrungen?

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдпрдГ

(рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ (рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгрдГ) рд╢реЛрднрдирдкрддрдирд╢реАрд▓рд╛ рд░рд╢реНрдордпреЛ рдпрд╕реНрдпред рд╕реБрдкрд░реНрдгрд╛ рдЗрддрд┐ рд░рд╢реНрдорд┐рдирд╛рдорд╕реБ рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдердГ

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬHe has lighted up the eight points of the horizon, the three regions of living beings, the seven rivers; may the golden-eyes Savit─Б come hither, bestowing upon the offerer of the oblation desirable riches.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The eight humps of the earth he has surveyed, the three wastelands three wagon-treks (wide), the seven rivers.
Golden-eyed god Savitar has come hither, establishing desirable treasures for the pious man.

Jamison Brereton Notes

In b I read tr─л╠Бwith both dh├бnva and y├│jan─Б (taking both as neut. pl.). The position of the numeral favors taking it with dh├бnva, which could, however, be singular; in favor of reading the numeral (also) with y├│jan─Б is X.86.20 dh├бnva ca y├бt krnt├бtram ca, k├бti svit t ╠е ─Б╠Бv├н y├│jan─Б тАЬWasteland and chasm – how many yojanas (of distance) are they away (from here).тАЭ (Note that dh├бnva is singular in that passage.)

Griffith

The earth’s eight points his brightness hath illumined, three desert regions and the Seven Rivers.
God Savitar the gold-eyed hath come hither, giving choice treasures unto him who worships.

Geldner

Er ├╝berschaut die acht Spitzen der Erde, die drei Ebenen meilenweit, die sieben Str├╢me. Der goldaugige Gott Savitri ist gekommen, der dem Opferspender die begehrenswerten Kleinode bringt.

Grassmann

Er hat bestrahlt der Erde acht Gebirge, drei Strecken Landes und die sieben Str├╢me, Gott Savitar mit goldnen Augen nahte, dem frommen Diener sch├╢ne Sch├дtze spendend.

Elizarenkova

рдЕрдиреНрд╡рдп: рдкреБрдирд░реЗрддрд╕реНрдп рдХреГрддреНрдпрдореБрдкрджрд┐рд╢реНрдпрдиреНрддреЗред

(рдЕрд╖реНрдЯреМ) рдЪрддрд╕реНрд░реЛрджрд┐рд╢ рдЙрдкрджрд┐рд╢рд╢реНрдЪ (рд╡рд┐) рд╡рд┐рд╢реЗрд╖рд╛рд░реНрдереЗ рдХреНрд░рд┐рдпрд╛рдпреЛрдЧреЗ (рдЕрдЦреНрдпрд╛рддреН) рдЦреНрдпрд╛рдкрдпрддрд┐ Wilson

English translation:

тАЬThe gold-handed, all-beholding, Savit─Б travels between the two regions of heaven and earth, dispels diseases, approaches the sun, and overspreads the sky with gloom, alternating radiance.тАЭ

Commentary by S─Бyaс╣Зa: с╣Ъgveda-bh─Бс╣гya

S┼лryam abhiveti: yadyevatayor ekadevat─Бtvam tath─Бpi m┼лrttibhedena gantс╣Ыgantavya-bh─Бvaс╕е: thought Savit─Б and S┼лrya are the same as regards their divinity, yet they are two different forms, and therefore, one may go to the other

Jamison Brereton

Golden-palmed Savitar, whose boundaries are distant, shuttles between both, both heaven and earth.
He thrusts away affliction; he pursues the sun; he reaches to heaven
through the black realm.

Griffith

The golden-handed Savitar, far-seeing, goes on his way between the earth and heaven,
Drives away sickness, bids the Sun approach us, and spreads the bright sky through the darksome region.

Geldner

Savitri mit der goldenen Hand, der Ausgezeichnete, f├дhrt zwischen beiden, zwischen Himmel und Erde. Er vertreibt die Krankheit, treibt die Sonne an; er reicht mit dem schwarzen Dunst bis an den Himmel.

Grassmann

Gott Savitar mit seinen goldnen H├дnden geht gesch├дftig wirkend zwischen Erd’ und Himmel hin, Vertreibt Bedr├дngniss, f├╝hrt herauf den Sonnengott, durch dunkeln Luftraum eilet er zum Himmel hin.

Elizarenkova

Wilson

English translation:

тАЬMay the golden-handed, life-bestowing, well-guiding, exhilarating, and affluent Savit─Б, be present (at the sacrifice); for the deity, if worshipped in the evening, it at hand, driving away r─Бkс╣гas and y─Бtudh─Бnas.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

The golden-handed lord of good guidance, of good grace, of good helpтАФlet him drive in our direction.
Repelling demons and sorcerers, the god has taken his place facing
evening, while being hymned.

Jamison Brereton Notes

On sv├бv─Бm╠Рas nom. sg. of the -s-stem sv-├бvas-, see AiG III.287. The Pp.

analyses it rather as sv├б-v─Бn тАШpossessing propertyтАЩ. Curiously Macdonell (Ved.

Reader, ad loc.) claims to be following the Pp., but tr. тАШaiding wellтАЩ.

Most tr. take pratidoс╣г├бm as a temporal, тАЬtowards eveningтАЭ or тАЬevery evening.тАЭ I think rather that itтАЩs spatial, construed naturally with ├бsth─Бt тАШtook his place, stoodтАЩ.

The god is facing west. (Cf. Peter Pan: тАЬstraight on тАШtil morning,тАЭ presumably meaning тАШeastтАЩ.) The same expression, also of Savitar, is found in VI.71.4, though it does not clinch the interpretation.

Griffith

May he, gold-handed Asura, kind Leader, come hither to us with his help and favour.
Driving off Raksasas and Yatudhanas, the God is present, praised in hymns at evening.

Geldner

Der Asura mit der goldenen Hand, der gute Weiser, der Barmherzige, Hilfreiche soll herw├дrts kommen. Die Unholde und Zauberer abwehrend steht der Gott allabendlich da, der Gepriesene.

Grassmann

Der Gott mit goldnen H├дnden, sicher leitend, er komme her mit sch├╢ner Huld und H├╝lfe; Gespenster und die Zauberer vertilgend erhob der Gott sich, abendlich gepriesen.

Elizarenkova

English translation:

тАЬYour paths, Savit─Б, are prepared of old, and free from dust, and well plural ced in the firmament; (coming) by those paths easy to be traversed, preserve us today. Deity, speak to us.тАЭ

Jamison Brereton

Your age-old paths, Savitar, dustless, well-made in the midspace, along these easily passable paths (come) to us today. Both guard us and speak on our behalf, o god.
The next eight hymns (I.36тАУ43) are attributed to Kaс╣Зva Ghaura, and the Kaс╣Зva family is named a number of times in this sequence. It is noteworthy that this collec tion does not contain a hymn to Indra. However, there are three hymns (I.37тАУ39) to the Maruts, IndraтАЩs regular companions, and the following hymn, I.40, is dedicated to Brahmaс╣Зaspati. Indra figures prominently in that hymn and is in fact identified with Brahmaс╣Зaspati in it.
For the most part the style of these hymns is uncomplex but nicely balanced.

Jamison Brereton Notes

Although it is possible to construe c directly with d, it seems best, following Geldner, to supply a verb of motion in c. The d p─Бda has a close parallel in I.114.10, suggesting that it is independent.

Note the unusual duplication of the nominal referent in both rel. and main clause: y├й тАж p├бnth─Бс╕е тАж / t├йbhiс╕е тАж path├нbhiс╕е.

Griffith

O Savitar, thine ancient dustless pathways are well established in the air’s mid-region:
O God, come by those paths so fair to travel, preserve thou us from harm this day, and bless us.

Deine fr├╝heren Pfade, die staublosen, wohlbereiteten in der Luft, o Savitri, auf diesen wegsamen Pfaden komm auch heute zu uns; sch├╝tze uns und segne uns, o Gott!

Auf deinen Pfaden, Savitar, den alten, die staublos sind und sch├╢ngebahnt im Luftraum, Die sch├╢n zu gehn sind, komm auf denen heute, und sch├╝tze uns, o Gott, und sprich uns Muth ein.

рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рд╣рд┐) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░ рддреНрд╡рдпрд╛ рдпреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд╛рджрд┐ рд▓реЛрдХрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рднреНрд░рдордгрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгрд┐рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рдп рдЪ рдзрд░реНрдордорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛ рдЕрдиреНрддрд░рд┐рдХреНрд╖реЗ рд╕реНрд╡рдорд╣рд┐рдореНрдирд┐ рдЪ рд░рдЪрд┐рддрд╛рд╕реНрддреЗрд╖реНрд╡рд┐рдореЗ рдпрдерд╛рдирд┐рдпрдордВ рднреНрд░рдордиреНрддрд┐ рд╡рд┐рдЪрд░рдиреНрддрд┐ рдЪ рддрд╛рдиреН рд╕рд░реНрд╡реЗрд╖рд╛рдВ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдВрд╢реНрдЪрд╛рд╕реНрдорднреНрдпрдВ рдмреНрд░реВрд╣рд┐ред рдпреЗрди рд╡рдпрдВ рдХрджрд╛рдЪрд┐рджрд┐рддрд╕реНрддрддреЛ рди рднреНрд░рдореЗрдореЗрддрд┐ реерезрезрее рдЕрд╕реНрдорд┐рдиреН рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЗ рд╕реВрд░реНрдпрд▓реЛрдХреЗрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╡рд╛рдпреБрдЧреБрдгрд╛рдирд╛рдВ рдкреНрд░рддрд┐рдкрд╛рджрдирд╛рд╢реНрдЪрддреБрд╕реНрддреНрд░рд┐рдВрд╢рд╕реВрдХреНрддреЛрдХреНрддрд╛рд░реНрдереЗрди рд╕рдВрдЧрддрд┐рд░рд╕реНрддреАрддрд┐ рд╡реЗрджрд┐рддрд╡реНрдпрдореНред рдЗрддрд┐ рен рд╡рд░реНрдЧрдГ рен рдЕрдиреБрд╡рд╛рдХрдГ рейрел рд╕реВрдХреНрддрдВ рдЪ рд╕рдорд╛рдкреНрддрдореН рее

рд╕рд╡рд┐рддрд╛ рдЬреЛрд╢реА тЖР рджрдпрд╛рдирдиреНрдж-рд╕рд░рд╕реНрд╡рддреА (рдо) - рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдердГ

рднрд╛рд╡рд╛рд░реНрдерднрд╛рд╖рд╛рдГ - рд╣реЗ рдИрд╢реНрд╡рд░рд╛! рддреВ рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдЧреЛрд▓рд╛рдВрдирд╛ рдлрд┐рд░рдгреНрдпрд╛рд╕рд╛рдареА рд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреНрдпрд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рд╕реБрдЦрд╛рд╕рд╛рдареА рдЖрдХрд╛рд╢ рд╡ рдЖрдкрд▓реНрдпрд╛ рдорд╣рд┐рдорд╛рдордпреА рдЬрдЧрд╛рдд рд╢реБрджреНрдз рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧ рдирд┐рд░реНрдорд╛рдг рдХреЗрд▓реЗрд▓реЗ рдЖрд╣реЗрд╕, рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдд рд╕реВрд░реНрдп рдЗрддреНрдпрд╛рджреА рдЧреЛрд▓ рдирд┐рдпрдорд╛рдиреЗ рдлрд┐рд░рддрд╛рдд рд╡ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдкреНрд░рд╛рдгреА рддреНрдпрд╛рдд рд╡рд╛рд╡рд░рддрд╛рдд. рддреНрдпрд╛ рд╕рд░реНрд╡ рдкрджрд╛рд░реНрдерд╛рдВрдЪреНрдпрд╛ рдорд╛рд░реНрдЧрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рд╡ рдЧреБрдгрд╛рдВрдЪрд╛ рдЙрдкрджреЗрд╢ рдХрд░ рдЬреНрдпрд╛рдореБрд│реЗ рдЖрдореНрд╣реА рдЗрдХрдбреЗ рддрд┐рдХрдбреЗ рднрдЯрдХрддрд╛ рдХрд╛рдорд╛ рдирдпреЗ. рее резрез рее
